  2
For U-Plane separate priorities can be supported based on ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid  (or the equivalent fields in RoE packet 3
headers).  This allows for different prioritization of some channels (e.g. PRACH/ SRS), or services (URLLC).  This 4
requires the ability to configure priority assignments to ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid via M -Plane messages.   The default U-5
Plane priority can be applied to flows not specifically configured with a different value via the M -Plane.  If a node does 6
not support configurable ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid priorities, then all U-Plane traffic will use the default value. 7
QoS failure (dropped packets) may be detected using the sequence numbers that make up part of the transport header.  8
Loss of a packet in the U-Plane will generally impact only a specific symbol except in rare cases where a multi -symbol 9
U-Plane message is sent (using the “symInc” field).  Loss of a C-Plane packet is more serious, with the possibility of 10
impacting an entire slot’s worth of data.  A broader impact is also possible with C-Plane packet loss: if downloaded 11
beamforming weights, beamforming attributes, or channel information is lost then a beamId may be incorrectly 12
associated with an “old” set of beamforming weights thereby possibly impacting multiple slots.  However, packet loss 13
can be detected via the sequence number so a recovery action may be taken to re-send messages that may have a 14
persistent impact. 15
3.4 Data Flow Identification 16
Differentiation between U/C-Plane and Management Plane traffic can be achieved using the following options:  17
• Data flow separation based on TCP/UDP (applicable when layer 3 transport is used for the C/U-plane) 18
• Data flow separation based on VLAN (applicable when layer 2 or layer 3 is used for the C/U -plane transport) 19
o Note: The mechanism for assigning VLAN ID to U-Plane and C-Plane is assumed to be via the M-Plane 20
• Data flow separation based on usage of different MAC addresses (applicable when Layer 2 is used for C/U plane 21
transport) 22
o e.g., separate MAC address used for M-Plane and U-Plane, or for baseband load sharing purposes 23
• Data flow separation based on different EtherTypes (applicable when Layer 2 is used for C/U plane transport) 24
The U-plane application also needs to uniquely associate different data flows (e.g. spatial streams) each with a 25
unique U/C plane endpoint address. This can be achieved in an O-RU using the eAxC identifier, and in the O-DU 26
using the eAxC identifier in combination with transport-based endpoint identifiers to differentiate O-RUs. In 27
addition, O-RU data flows can be switched/routed to different O-DUs (or different O-DU ports or O-DU 28
processors) according to the transport-based identifiers associated with an eAxCid (referred to as processing-29
elements in the WG4 M-Plane Specification) to allow frames/packets to be switched/routed by network equipment 30
with no visibility of the eAxC values carried in the eCPRI/1914.3 header. 31
 Different transport identifiers (e.g. UDP/IP, VLAN, MAC) can be used based on whether layer 2 or layer 3 transport is 32
used for the U/C plane: 33
• U/C-plane data flow separation using UDP-port identifiers (applicable when layer 3 transport is used for the C/U-34
plane) 35
• U/C-plane data flow separation using on VLAN identities (applicable when layer 2 or layer 3 is used for the C/U -36
plane transport) 37

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      54
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
• U/C-plane data flow separation based on usage of different MAC addresses (applicab le when Layer 2 is used for 1
C/U plane transport) 2
 3
3.5 Fragmentation 4
Fragmentation is applied in case data (U-Plane or C-Plane data) with Ethernet transport overheads to be transferred 5
exceed maximum transmission unit (MTU) of the network. This specificatio n allows two methods for fragmentation, 6
application layer fragmentation and transport layer fragmentation: 7
3.5.1 Application layer fragmentation 8
• Application creates C-plane or U-Plane messages, which when including overheads can fit to MTU 9
requirements set by network 10
• Sequence ID: Sequence ID increases for every message, E=1, Subsequence ID=0  11
An example of application fragmentation is provided in Figure 3-10, wherein a long data section is split between 12
multiple U-Plane messages.  In the example it is a single data section (0xABC) so described as such in the C -Plane, and 13
in the U-Plane the sectionId is cited multiple times in the multiple U-Plane messages but with differing and consecutive 14
groups of PRBs as indicated by the startPrbu and numPrbu fields.  The I and Q word width in the example is 14 bits, 15
which for such a large data section requires multiple U-Plane messages.  The ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid (0xDEF3) is shown 16
with a random example value, as is the sequence ID in the C-Plane (0x99) and independently in the U-Plane (0x40-17
0x48). 18
 19
 20
Figure 3-10 : Example of Application-Level Fragmentation of U-Plane Messages 21
 22
3.5.2 Radio Transport layer (eCPRI or IEEE-1914.3) fragmentation 23
o Application creates U-Plane messages, which when including overhead may exceed MTU 24
requirements set by network 25
o Radio transport layer splits message which may contain more than one section into pieces such that 26
the fragments with overheads fit to MTU requirements set by network. 27
o Sequence ID: Sequence ID remains same for all the fragments. Subsequence ID starts from 0 for the 28
first fragment and counts up for each fragment. Last fragment flagged with E=1, others E=0.  29
 30
  31

3.5.3 Fragmentation Guideline 3
Application layer fragmentation should be applied so that maximum size standard IEEE 802.3 Ethernet frames can be 4
used. (Jumbo frames, if used, increase the maximum MTU size). 5
• In case of L2 only solution, application layer maximum transmission unit size is  standard IEEE 802.3 Ethernet 6
frame payload size (1500 bytes) – transport overhead (8 bytes) = 1492 bytes (or larger for Jumbo frames) 7
When a U-plane section payload is fragmented due to large number of PRBs, it will be divided into multiple groups of 8
PRBs such that each group (including the application headers) can fit to the MTU requirements. Each group of PRBs 9
shall have its respective control fields including the same section ID from the C-plane and startPrbu and numPrbu to 10
identify its contents (See Figure 3-9).  When an application layer message exceeds the MTU size set via the M-Plane 11
configuration, radio-transport layer fragmentation can be applied at the transport layer and has the advantage of 12
allowing application layer messages to fit whatever is the MTU size without the application having to know about 13
transport-level details.  14
  15

Chapter 5 C-plane Protocol 1
5.1 General 2
5.2 Function 3
5.2.1 C-Plane Transport 4
Either eCPRI or IEEE 1914.3 is used as an encapsulation mechanism for the control-plane messages. Due to the nature 5
of these messages (very strict delay constraints), it is assumed that message acknowledgements are not possible . 6
Likewise, it is assumed that a different data flow is used other than the U-Plane channel. Further, C-Plane messages are 7
not concatenated with U-Plane messages within same Ethernet frame. 8
5.3 Elementary Procedures 9
5.3.1 Scheduling and Beamforming Commands Transfer procedure 10
This procedure is used to exchange C-Plane messages between O-DU and O-RU. The main purpose of these messages 11
is to transmit data-associated control information required for processing of user data (e.g., scheduling  and 12
beamforming commands) if such information is not provided via M-Plane (see section 6.2.2 for more details). Messages 13
are sent separately for DL related commands and UL related commands (see Figure 5-1).  See also Figure 5-8 for the 14
special case of LTE LAA wherein there are UL as well as DL C-Plane message flows.  For purpose of increased 15
flexibility, C-Plane messages may be sent either jointly or separately depending on the channel for which information is 16
conveyed. For example, PUCCH and PUSCH may be bundled or not bundled into a single C -Plane message depending 17
on implementation.  18

5.3.2 Mixed Numerology and PRACH Handling 1
5G NR defines Physical Resource Block (PRB) where the number of subcarriers per PRB is the same for all 2
numerologies (twelve). However, subcarrier spacing may differ, resulting in mixed numerology used in time and 3
frequency domains respectively. Likewise, mixed numerologies may be applied to both DL and UL respectively 4
(Figure 5-2). 5
 6
Figure 5-2 : Mixed Numerology in Time and Frequency Domain 7
Frequency indexing across multiple numerologies  8
• RB indexing (i.e. the physical resource block) is always dependent on the used numerology. For PRACH and 9
SSB the relation is with the physical channel. In case of PRACH, indexing of RBs inside of each PRACH 10
frequency block follows 3GPP specifications and PRACH subcarrier extraction is performed in the O-DU. In 11
particular, the first RE of the first RB addressed inside section Id shall correspond  with the first guard tone 12
used at the lower edge of the PRACH frequency block based on the PRACH SCS. The O-RU, using the filter 13
index and SCS of corresponding PUSCH, knows the PRACH subcarrier position and guard tones and can then 14
adjust its filtering parameters (e.g. filter center, passband). For the SSB case, its own separate frequency offset 15
is assigned.  16
Figure 5-3 shows a PRACH example illustrating startPrbc, numPrbc, and freqOffset. Specifically,  17
o freqOffset indicate the location of lowest RE’s center in the lowest RB defined by frameStructure, 18
with respect to center-of-channel-bandwidth. 19
o startPrbc and numPrbc in the section type 3 indicate the PRB in the RB grid defined by corresponding 20
freqOffset and frameStructure. 21
o Note that numPrbc may exclude PRBs with all-guard-tones at the upper end of the PRACH frequency 22
block. (Hence, in the example in Figure 5-3, numPrbc could be set to 71 or 72). 23

Slot indexing with mixed numerologies 7
For a given frequency range FR1 or FR2, the highest possible numerology supported by the O-RU shall be used as the 8
common reference per component carrier for the start of the slot identified by slotId.  UL and DL on the same 9
component carrier shall use the same reference numerology for slotId.  If the highest numerology supported by the O-10
RU allows both normal and extended CP then normal CP shall be used as reference. Note that the O-RU shall advance 11
slots with extended CP against the reference.  The symbol duration and position in time is calculated from the µ value 12
(SCS from frameStruture in message field or configured via M-plane) and the slotId field in the CU-Plane message.   13
The value of the sectionId field in CU-Plane messages addressed per eAxC shall be unique per slot identified by slotId 14
value. 15
For example, in FR1 case, the maximum slot numbers per subframe is four, when the maximum supported SCS by the 16
O-RU is 60kHz 17

PRACH formats with multiple repetitions of preamble 11

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      63
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
Certain PRACH formats lead to PRACH symbols to be constructed from multiple repet itions of a preamble sequence, 1
with only the Cyclic Prefix (CP) used with the first sequence. Therefore, the O-RU must be informed how to correctly 2
execute CP extraction and FFT.  This is achieved by sending a single control message spanning over multiple symbols 3
(e.g. example depicted in Figure 5-6: number of symbols = 4, CP length = 0, time offset duration is adjusted by an 4
equivalent time value of 1152 samples to compensate for setting CP length =0), which reduces the number of C-Plane 5
messages and data sections required.  6
Optionally O-RU can advertise the list of the supported formats for the specific endpoint. If the O-RU chooses not to, it 7
means O-RU supports all PRACH formats and the O-DU may select whatever format that is 3GPP compliant with the 8
selected SCS. If the O-RU implements earlier releases of the M-plane specification which does not support such 9
reporting, then the negotiation of PRACH formats to use must happen offline, i.e. operator s and/or vendors have to 10
ensure that the intended PRACH formats are supported by both O-RU and O-DU. 11
 12
The example in Figure 5-7 depicts the scenario with format A2 and 30kHz SCS, in which only CP extraction occurs 13
once, yet there are four associated FFT operations. 14
 15
Figure 5-7 : Example of PRACH Format A2 16

• One way to implement precoding in the O-RU is via the beamID values, wherein a beamID points to a 2
beamforming vector that also implements the precoding operation. 3
5.3.4 LAA Commands Transfer procedure 4
This procedure is used to exchange C-Plane messages between O-DU and O-RU. The main purpose of these messages 5
is to support LAA feature in the O-RU/O-DU.  See Annex G for more details on the LAA message flow. 6
5.3.4.1 LBT procedure overview  7
The LBT procedure is used to configure the O-RU with the parameters needed to do LBT prior to PDSCH or DRS 8
transmission OTA. The O-RU needs to report the LBT process outcome (either success or failure) in the indication 9
message.  10
In contrast to licensed spectrum, where the O-RU may continuously send data or reference signals OTA, in unlicensed 11
spectrum, the O-RU can only send discontinuous bursts of data (of length MCOT) or periodic DRS signals. The 12
LBT_DL_CONFIG request message is sent once prior to each OTA transmission on the LAA SCell. This includes both 13
DRS and PDSCH (i.e., MCOT burst) transmissions. For every LBT_DL_CONFIG  request message, the O-RU replies 14
with the LBT_DL indication messages which include the LBT outcome and the status of the subframe 15
(transmitted/dropped) (see Figure 5-8). 16
If O-RU can manage a congestion window by itself, the O-DU does not need to send LBT_DL_CONFIG request 17
message to start the LBT procedure at O-RU. Because O-RU can determine the start timing of LBT procedure, the 18
requirements of O-DU for the LBT procedure at the O-RU is a delivery of needed information to adjust a congestion 19
window managed by O-RU. To transmit these information, O-DU sends LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ message, and O-RU 20
notifies to the O-DU by LBT_CWCONFIG_RSP message to indicate that the LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ mess age is 21
successfully received or not. Also, O-RU can adjust its congestion window based on the information on the 22
LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ message.  For every LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ request message, the O-RU replies with the 23
LBT_DL indication message(s) which include the LBT outcome and the status of the subframe (transmitted/dropped). 24
For the DRS signal, initially, the O-DU must configure the O-RU with the DRS parameters (DMTC period and DMTC 25
offset) via the M-plane. 26
Before every DRS period, the O-DU must send the LBT_DL_CONFIG request message and the DRS signal. O-RU 27
does LBT and transmits the DRS signal OTA in case of LBT success. The O-RU then must send the LBT_DL 28
indication. 29
The DRS signal can be transmitted over the fronthaul interface similar to other reference signals such as the 30
PSS/SSS/CRS.  31

5.3.4.2 Definitions 4
• 𝐷𝑂𝑊: Maximum one-way fronthaul latency 5
• 𝑃𝐷𝑈: Maximum O-DU processing time (reading an upstream O-RU c-plane message, MAC processing, 6
sending the downstream U-plane data) 7
• 𝑃𝑅𝑈: Maximum O-RU processing time (sending an upstream c-plane message, receiving downstream U-plane 8
data, transmitting U-plane data OTA)  9
• 𝐵𝑅𝑈: O-RU Buffer depth (for LAA) ceiled to an integer number of OFDM symbols in microseconds (up to 140 10
symbols, for example (i.e., MCOT)). This is equivalent to the minimum amount of data that must be buffered 11
at the O-RU. This parameter could be less than or equal to the actual O-RU buffer size communicated via the 12
M-Plane.  13
• Expired symbol: Symbol where the current time at the O-RU exceeds its target transmission time (i.e., 14
SFN/SF) OTA.  15
• Normal (partially-filled) SF assumption: 𝑇𝑠𝑡𝑎𝑟𝑡 is the start of the transmission time, which occurs at the first SF 16
(slot) boundary the O-RU encounters after starting the LBT CAT 4 process and after finishing the minimum 17
sensing duration. Initially known to the O-DU (since it sends the LBT start time and the LBT parameters to the 18
O-RU). It can be updated in real-time based on the LBT outcome and the communication between the O-DU 19
and O-RU.  Note that here, a “slot” follows the LTE definition of containing seven symbols. 20

5.3.4.3 General Guidelines for the LAA-procedure 10
5.3.4.3.1 PDSCH Transmission 11
• O-DU should avoid buffer overflow or underflow at the O-RU: 12
• O-DU should only send 𝐵𝑅𝑈 worth of data to the O-RU for every single transmission 13
• O-DU should plan for the data to be received at the O-RU only 𝑃𝑅𝑈 before the actual OTA 14
transmission time at the O-RU 15
• O-RU should avoid buffer overflow or underflow at the O-RU: 16
• O-RU should flush its buffer (by dropping any expired symbols) as soon as any s ymbol becomes 17
expired (i.e., current time is larger than the symbol’s scheduled time) 18
• O-RU should immediately send a success LBT indication to the O-DU once the channel is acquired.  19
• The O-RU should send an error message to the O-DU if data received is larger than its local buffer  20
• The O-RU should send a subframe drop or transmission message to the O-DU when buffered 21
subframe is dropped because scheduled time is passed, or is transmitted after LBT success.  22
• The O-RU should have a buffer that satisfies the following equation: 𝐵𝑅𝑈 ≥2×𝐷𝑂𝑊 +𝑃𝐷𝑈 +𝑃𝑅𝑈 23
• Note on LBT CAT 4 in general: 24
• The O-DU can configure the O-RU (via the M-plane) with the threshold on the LBT CAT 4 duration 25
(e.g., 8 ms). Once this threshold has exceeded, the O-RU sends a failure LBT indication to the O-DU, 26

For the NR case, data symbol numbering in a slot shall be from zero to thirteen (for extended CP, eleven).  For LTE the 33
symbol numbering shall be mapped to the NR numbering as follows: 34

 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖+1 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′ =7+𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 37
LTE with extended prefix the following applies: 38
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′=𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 39
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖+1 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′ =6+𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 40

5.3.6 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) 4
Dynamic Spectrum sharing allows different technologies – 4G LTE and 5G NR in this version of the specification, to 5
share same frequency carrier dynamically, i.e. the O-DU may allocate one or more set(s) of frequency-time resources 6
(or PRBs) to LTE or NR dynamically. The O-RU also must support this feature for the O-DU to take advantage of such 7
an allocation. This version of the specification supports DSS via using dedicated eAxC ids (i.e. endpoints) for LTE and 8
NR or via using Section Extension =9 for DSS. 9
5.3.6.1 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) via Dedicated Endpoints 10
Dedicated endpoints are configured in the O-RU for LTE and NR (hence dedicated eAxC ids) to implement DSS. For 11
e.g. when an O-DU allocates a set of PRBs for LTE, O-DU uses an eAxC id dedicated for LTE (assigned to a carrier 12
identified as an LTE carrier) to address the LTE endpoint; at a different time when the O-DU allocates the same set of 13
PRBs for NR, the O-DU uses eAxC id dedicated for NR (assigned to a carrier identified as an NR carrier) to address the 14
NR endpoint in the O-RU.  15
When using this approach, a carrier will be assigned to LTE or NR, so when both LTE and NR are to be supported at 16
the same time (“DSS”), two carriers with overlapping frequency ranges are to be identified, one being LTE and the 17
other being NR.  It will be up to the O-RU to overlap the two carriers such that the same frequency range can support 18
both NR and LTE, and it will be up to the O-DU to assure that no RE is assigned to both LTE and NR at the same time. 19
5.3.6.2 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) via Section Extension =9 for DSS 20
Using Section Extension =9 for DSS, the O-DU can use a single eAxC id (and hence a single endpoint) for conveying 21
LTE and NR PRB allocations if the O-RU is capable of handling both LTE and NR processing using one endpoint (i.e. 22
the O-RU indicates support for Section Extension =9). Note that a single carrier may be allocated to either LTE, NR or 23
both, and supporting DSS in this manner means the carrier (to which the endpoint is assigned) would be designated as 24
supporting both.  The O-DU indicates whether the PRB allocation information is applicable to LTE or to NR via 25
Section Extension =9.   26
5.4 Elements for the C-plane Protocol 27
5.4.1 General 28
C-Plane messages are encapsulated using a two-layered header approach. The first layer consists of a eCPRI common 29
header or IEEE 1914.3 common header, including corresponding fields used to indicate the message type, while the 30
second layer is an application layer including necessary fields for control and synchronization.  Within the application 31
layer, a “section” defines the characteristics of U-plane data to be transferred or received from a beam with one pattern 32
id.  In general, the transmission header, application header, and sections are all intended to be aligned on 4 -byte 33
boundaries and are transmitted in “network byte order” meaning the most significant byte of a multi-byte parameter is 34
transmitted first. 35
When the optional “little endian byte order” is chosen via M-plane, the beamforming weights (Section Type 1 or 3, and 36
extType = 1) and ciIsample/ciQsample (Section Type 6) fields shall use little endian byte order to transmit the complex 37
numbers. Annex D.1 shows little endian byte order format for various I/Q data length.  38
Table 5-2 described the section types are supported within the C-Plane. 39
Table 5-2 : Section Types 40

symbols in Downlink or Uplink

used (idle periods, guard periods). Likewise, there are no associated
U-Plane messages containing IQ data for this Section Type. The
purpose is to inform the O-RU that transmissions may be halted

during the specified idle interval for e.g. power-savings or to provide

5.4.1.1 Section Extensions 3
Within a data section the section header in most cases includes a “extension flag” which indicates parameters that apply 4
to the section beyond those within the section header (the extension flag is most often adjacent to the beamId or ueId 5
fields).  The presence of this extension flag indicates that following the header a section extension is present.  Within 6
the section extension is another extension flag, adjacent to the “extType” field, which indicates that a second  (or third, 7
etc.) extension is present.  In this way any number of section extensions may be included within a data section.  This 8
provides an extensibility for section parameters without the need to continually redefine the section header or create 9
new section types to accommodate future fronthaul specification needs. 10
The section extension takes the form reminiscent of “TLV”: there is a type field specifically “extType” which is a 7 -bit 11
field describing the specific extension type, then a one-byte length field specifically “extLen” field detailing how many 12
4-byte words are contained in the extension (minimum of 1 including the “extType” and “extLen” fields), and then 13
some number of parameters that depend on the “extType” value for their definition.  In all cases the section extension 14
will be an integer number of (4-byte) words in length. 15
Specific valid values of “extType”, their meanings and their associated parameters are detailed in subsequent sub -16
chapters of this spec.  17
5.4.1.2 Coupling of C-Plane and U-Plane 18
Selected types of C-Plane messages (section types 1, 3 and 5) carry data section descriptions that convey information 19
applicable to data sections carried in U-Plane messages. This chapter describes a method of coupling data section 20
descriptions from C-Plane and data sections in U-Plane. 21
5.4.1.2.1 Coupling via sectionId Value 22
This method of C-Plane and U-Plane coupling is used by default. O-DU may configure O-RU to use the other method 23
via M-Plane. In this method information from section description D in C-Plane message CM is applied to resource 24
element R in PRB P (PRB understood as 12 resource elements of one OFDM symbol consecutive in frequency) in data 25
section S in U-Plane message UM if: 26
1. CM corresponds to UM i.e. both have the same eAxC_id and CM.dataDirection value matches direction of 27
UM 28
2. CM.frameId = UM.frameId and CM.subframeId = UM.subframeId and CM.slotId = UM.slotId  29
3. symbol identified by UM.symbolId is described by the section description D.  30
This requires evaluation of CM.startSymbolId, symInc and numSymbol in CM or checking D.symbolMask 31
in section extension #6 if this extension is present. 32
4. PRB p is described by the section description D. This requires checking that D.startPrbc ≤ P < D.startPrbc + 33
D.numPrbc ∙ (D.rb + 1), if D.rb = 1 checking that D.startPrbc modulo 2 = P modulo 2; it requires 34
evaluating D.rbgMask in section extension type #6 if this extension is present in D. 35

5. D.reMask has value 1 in a bit corresponding to RE R 1
6. D.sectionId = S.sectionId 2

4. Sender of C-Plane shall order section descriptions such that any section descriptions referencing to any RE 32

value in reMask). This allows O-RU to more quickly identify section descriptions that carry beamforming 34
configuration for any RE and also makes them localized in memory which can improve message processing 35
performance.  36

O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
4. PRB p is described by the section description D. This requires checking that D.startPrbc ≤ P < D.startPrbc + 1
D.numPrbc ∙ (D.rb + 1), if D.rb = 1 checking that D.startPrbc modulo 2 = P modulo 2; it requires 2
evaluating D.rbgMask in section extension type #6 if this extension is present in D. 3
5. D.reMask has value 1 in a bit corresponding to RE R and D has highest priority among data section 4
descriptions referencing the RE R in the message CM. Priority of data section description is the value of 5
priority field in section extension type #6 (see 5.4.7.6.4) if this extension is present in D and zero if the 6
extension is absent. Note: scope of search for highest priority description is restricted to one C -Plane message 7
to avoid beamforming configuration errors that would be unavoidable if scope would be covering multiple 8
messages and one of them would be lost. See also note in restriction #3 below. 9
In addition, the following restrictions apply (in context of one eAxC): 10
1. A PRB may occur only once in all U-Plane messages related to the same OFDM symbol. 11
2. Data section descriptions that refer to the same RE and are conveyed in the same C-Plane message shall have 12
different priority in order to avoid ambiguity. 13
3. If a complete beamforming configuration does not fit into one C-Plane message, then sender shall duplicate 14
highest priority data section descriptions, specifically each C-Plane message must contain the highest priority 15
section description referring to any RE that is referred in a message. This is required to ensure that O-RU will 16
interpret configuration received in each message correctly. If such duplication is needed to avoid 17
misinterpretation it does not violate restriction #4. 18
4. Sender shall avoid sending unnecessary data section descriptions e.g. descriptions that carry the same 19
configuration (but refer to note in restriction #3).  20
5. Sender of C-Plane shall send in sectionId a value 4095. 21
6. Sender of C-Plane shall order section descriptions such that any section descriptions referring to any RE (non -22
zero value of reMask) are present before section descriptions that do not  reference any RE (i.e. zero value in 23
reMask); section descriptions referring to any RE shall be ordered by effective priority (highest priority first). 24
Ordering section descriptions with non-zero reMask first allows O-RU to more quickly identify section 25
descriptions that carry beamforming configuration for any RE and also makes them localized in memory 26
which can improve message processing performance. Ordering section descriptions by highest priority first is 27
intended to optimize O-RU C-plane message processing i.e. RE beamforming configuration can be 28
determined from the earliest section description occurring in the message.  29
5.4.1.2.4 Coupling via Frequency and Time with Priorities (Optimized) 30
All the restrictions remain same as coupling via frequency and time with priorities except restriction 5 31
5. Sender of C-Plane shall send in sectionId value 4095 for section description with lower priority . For highest 32
priority sections unique sectionIds shall be set in a defined range  starting from “0” to “max-highest-priority-33
sections-per-slot” specified through M-Plane, across eAxC IDs (limiting this range helps O-RU reduce the 34
search space for repeated highest priority section descriptions detection). While duplicating highest priority 35
sections, all fields including sectionId shall be duplicated. 36
In addition to associating unique sectionId to highest priority section as described above, O-DU shall set the “repetition” 37
flag to “1” for every repeated C-Plane message. O-RU can choose to process or ignore the flag based on its implementation 38
(Section 5.4.7.6.5). 39
 40
5.4.2 Scheduling and Beamforming Commands  41
A common frame format is used for C-Plane messages, consisting of a transport layer and an application layer. The 42
application layer is within the transport layer payload and consists of a common header for time reference, followed by 43
information and parameters dependent and specific to the Section Type in use. Multiple sets of section data of the same 44
Section Type value can be lined up one after another within the payload. To minimize packet rate over the interface, 45
transmitter should fill messages with as many subsequent sections (with or without sequential section IDs) as possible. 46
However, sets of section data of different Section Type values are to be sent via separate messages (i.e. different values 47
of Section Type shall not be mixed within a single C-Plane message payload). 48

5.4.3 Coding of Information Elements – Transport Layer 5
See Section 3.1.3 for transport header information element details. 6
5.4.4 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Common 7
5.4.4.1 dataDirection (data direction (gNB Tx/Rx)) 8
Description: This parameter indicates the gNB data direction.  9
Value range: {0b=Rx (i.e. UL), 1b=Tx (i.e. DL)}. 10
Type: binary bit. 11
Field length: 1 bit. 12
 13
5.4.4.2 payloadVersion (payload version) 14
Description: This parameter defines the payload protocol version valid for the following IEs in the application layer. In 15
this version of the specification payloadVersion=001b shall be used.  16
Value range: {000b-111b=Payload version}. 17

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      84
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
Type: unsigned integer. 1
Field length: 3 bits. 2
Default Value: 001b (version 1 assumed). 3
 4
5.4.4.3 filterIndex (filter index) 5
Description: This parameter defines an index to the channel filter to be used between IQ data and air interface, both in 6
DL and UL. For most physical channels filterIndex =0000b is used which indexes the standard channel filter, e.g. 7
100MHz channel filter for 100MHz nominal carrier bandwidth. Another use case is PRACH in UL, where different 8
filter indices can be used for different PRACH formats, assuming that be fore FFT processing of PRACH data there is a 9
separate PRACH filter or PRACH filter in addition to the standard channel filter in UL. Please note that for PRACH , 10
when section type “3” message is used, there is typically also a frequency offset (see freqOffset) applied before the 11
PRACH filter.  12
NOTE: Filter index is commanded from O-DU to O-RU. Likewise, it is not mandatory to command special filters, and 13
filter index = 0000b is also allowed for PRACH. 14
NOTE: When using filter indices corresponding to PRACH, the first RE of the first PRB addressed inside the section Id 15
shall correspond with the first guard tone used at the lower edge of the PRACH frequency block as specified in 3GPP 16
RAN1 TS 3x.211. In case of fragmentation of 1 data section over multiple U -Plane messages, this is applicable to the 17
first fragmented section. 18
NOTE: Since different PRACH formats are assigned to the same filterIndex value, optionally O -RU can notify by M-19
plane the specific supported formats (grouped into PRACH format -groups) in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module on a per-20
endpoint basis. 21
Value range: {0000b-1111b}. 22

5.4.4.10 udCompHdr (user data compression header) 37
See section 6.3.3.13 for the description of this parameter. 38

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      86
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
The udCompHdr information is provided on the U-Plane, instructing the O-RU (on DL) and O-DU (on UL) how to 1
interpret and decompress the received U-Plane data.  However, the O-RU is not expected to decide by itself the best UL 2
data format and data compression method, instead the O-DU shall instruct the O-RU via udCompHdr in a C-Plane 3
message.  This means the udCompHdr in a C-Plane message only has meaning for UL U-Plane data (dataDirection = 4
0b) and should be set to 0x00 when dataDirection = 1b (DL data), and the receiving O-RU shall ignore the received 5
udCompHdr value.  When static data format and compression is used (see 6.1.2) then udCompHdr is not needed in any 6
C-Plane message and should be set to 0x00, and the receiving O-RU shall ignore the received udCompHdr value. 7
Note that it is impermissible to specify different values of udCompHdr for the same data section, even if it is sent over 8
separate C-Plane messages discriminated by different reMask values.  Only a single compression method per  data 9
section is supported (see section 5.4.5.1).   The O-RU response if the C-Plane specifies multiple udCompHdr values for 10
a single data section is undefined. 11

number of samples Ts (=1/30.72MHz as specified in 3GPP TS38.211 section 4.1).  The value shall be less than the slot 23
length. The slot length is based on the SCS on which the startSymbolId numerology is based (see Tables 5 -1 and 5-1a in 24
5.3.2). For the mixed numerology case (non-PRACH), timeOffset points to the same timing pointed by startSymbolId. 25
For PRACH, refer to section 2.3.2.  26
time_offset = timeOffset * ts 27

5.4.5 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Sections 1
5.4.5.1 sectionId (section identifier) 2
Description: If C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via sectionId (see 5.4.1.2.1) is used then this parameter identifies 3
individual data sections that are described by data section descriptions within the C-Plane message. The purpose of the 4
sectionId is to map U-Plane data sections to the corresponding C-Plane message (and Section Type) associated with the 5
data.  Two or more C-Plane data section descriptions with same SectionId may be cited corresponding to a single U-6
Plane data section containing a combined payload for both citations (e.g., for supporting mixed CSI RS and PDSCH). 7
This case is applicable when usage of reMask is complimentary (or orthogonal) and different beam directions (i.e. 8
beamIds) are given the resource elements.  Data sections are specific to a value of eAxC so different eAxC values may 9
have differently-defined data sections e.g. have different ranges of PRBs contained within.  10
NOTES:  11
▪ sectionIds are specific to a slot, so sectionId values may be “reused” for each slot, and the sectionId value for 12
one slot has no specified relation to the sectionId value for a different slot  13
▪ All data in section descriptions with same SectionId value shall have same rb, startPrbc, numPrbc, 14
udCompHdr, and numSymbol IE fields’ content.  15
▪ An upper bound on the max number of section IDs that can be addressed per eAxC or per sets of eAxCs, per 16
symbol and per slot, for DL and for UL respectively, shall be conveyed via M-plane messaging as part of the 17
O-RU capabilities description. 18
▪ The sectionId cited in a C-Plane message must have the same value as the sectionId in the corresponding U-19
Plane message for the given data section as defined by the frameId, subFrameId, slotId, startSymbolid fields 20
and range of relevant PRBs as indicated by the totality of the specified startPrb(c/u) an d numPrb(c/u) fields. 21
If C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via sectionId (see 5.4.1.2.1) is not used, then the sectionId value is not used for 22
identification of data sections in U-plane messages and is not used for identification of data section descriptions in C-23
plane messages. In this case above rules for uniqueness of sectionId value within slot and restriction on rb, startPrbc, 24
numPrbc, udCompHdr, and numSymbol IE fields’ content do not apply. Sender shall send SectionId = 4095. The only 25
exception to this is “Coupling via Frequency and Time with Priorities (Optimized)” where a unique value of sectionId is 26
still used for identification of the highest priority data section descriptions in C-plane messages (Sec 5.4.1.2.4, 27
restriction 5). The corresponding U-Plane messages shall still use sectionId value as 4095 in this case. 28
An upper bound on the maximum number of data section descriptions that can be addressed per eAxC or per sets of 29
eAxCs, per symbol and per slot, for DL and for UL respectively, shall be conveyed via M-plane messaging as part of 30
the O-RU capabilities description. 31
Value range: {0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111b}. 32
Type: unsigned integer. 33
Field length: 12 bits. 34
 35
5.4.5.2 rb (resource block indicator) 36
Description: This parameter is used to indicate if every RB is used or every other RB is used. The starting RB is 37
defined by startPrbc and total number of used RBs is defined by numPrbc.  Example: RB=1, startPrb=1, numPrb=3, 38
then the PRBs used are 1, 3, and 5.  If numPrbc=0 (i.e., all PRBs), then the sending node shall set the rb value to zero, 39
and the receiving node shall ignore whatever rb value is received and assume it is zero.  40
Value range: {0b=every RB used; 1b=every other RB used}. 41
Type: binary bit. 42
Field length: 1 bit. 43
Default Value: 0b (every RB used). 44
 45

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      89
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
5.4.5.3 symInc (symbol number increment command) 1
Description: This parameter is used to indicate which symbol number is relevant to the given section  description.  It is 2
expected that for each C-Plane message a symbol number is maintained and starts with the value of startSymbolid.  The 3
same value is used for each section in the message as long as symInc is zero.  When symInc is one, the maintained 4
symbol number should be incremented to the next symbol, and that new symbol number should be used for that section 5
and each subsequent section until the symInc bit is again detected to be one.  In the case of a multiple-symbol data 6
section (numSymbol > 1), the new symbol number shall be the one after the last symbol in the data section.  In this 7
manner, multiple symbols may be handled by a single C-Plane message.   8
A few other points regarding use of symInc in the C-Plane: 9
a) SymInc may be used when different data section descriptions have a different number of symbols under certain 10
conditions namely that the data section descriptions in the C-Plane message are carefully arranged.  The 11
arrangement must be such that the following procedure as applied by the O-RU works correctly: 12
symbol[s] - symbol addressed by section description s=1…N (considers section descriptions in one C -13
Plane message, s=1 identifies the first section description) shall be calculated as follows: 14
Let symInc[s] and numSymbols[s] are values of corresponding fields of section description s  15
For sake of simplicity let symbol[0] = startSymbolId, symInc[0]=0 and numSymbols[0]=1  16
for s=1…N (all section descriptions in a message) 17
If symInc[s] = 0 then symbol[s] = symbol[s-1]  18
Else symbol[s] = symbol[s-1] + numSymbols[s-1] 19
b) SymInc is specific to a data section description and, if section extension type #6 is not present, is affecting 20
range of symbols described by the section description. When C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via sectionId (see 21
5.4.1.2.1) is used and a data section is referenced by multiple data section descriptions (e.g. with different 22
reMask values) if the value of symInc is to be set to 1, then only the first invocation of the sectionId shall have 23
symInc=1 and all other invocations of the sectionId shall have symInc=0 in the same C -Plane message.  This 24
assures that the above rule can be applied (in the same C-Plane message only) while assuring that all 25
invocations of the data section descriptions will refer to the same symbols, which must be the case whether the 26
invocations are in the same C-Plane message or in separate C-Plane messages. 27
Use of symInc in the U-Plane is independent of the use of symInc in the C-Plane. The current view is that U-Plane 28
message includes data for a single symbol (to avoid degrading the latency performance of the U -Plane), so use of 29
symInc=1 is prohibited in the U-Plane as of this version of the specification. A future version may allow use of 30
symInc=1 in the U-Plane to allow multiple symbols to be contained in a single U-Plane message.  31
 32
Value range: {0b=use the current symbol number; 1b=increment the current symbol number and use that}.  33
Type: binary bit. 34
Field length: 1 bit. 35
Default Value: 0b (do not increment the current symbol number). 36
 37
5.4.5.4 startPrbc (starting PRB of data section description) 38
Description: This parameter is the starting PRB of a data section described in the C-Plane message.  Values of 39
startPrbc and numPrbc must ensure that data sections must never overlap: a single PRB may only exist within one data 40
section for a given value of eAxC.  For one C-Plane message, there may be multiple U-Plane messages associated with 41
it and requiring defining from which PRB the control commands are applicable.  42
Note: freqOffset affects the frequency span for specific range of PRB numbers. Therefore "must never overlap" must 43
consider the value of freqOffset. 44
Center frequency FRE in Hz of a subcarrier corresponding to RE #k (k = 0 … 11) in PRB identified by startPrbc is 45
defined by: 46
FRE = center_of_channel_bandwidth + frequency_offset + startPrbc * 12 * f + k * f + dc_skip 47
where  48

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      90
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
center_of_channel_bandwidth in Hz is configured in M-plane, 1
frequency_offset is calculated from freqOffset field (see 5.4.5.11) if freqOffset is present in the C -plane message or 2
calculated from M-plane parameter offset-to-absolute-frequency-center (in this case frequency_offset = offset-to-3
absolute-frequency-center * f * 0.5 where f is frequency in Hz corresponding to subcarrier spacing configured via 4
M-Plane) otherwise, 5
f is frequency in Hz corresponding to the subcarrier spacing configured in frameStructure (see 5.4.4.13) if 6
frameStructure is present in the message, or to the subcarrier spacing configured via M -Plane otherwise, 7
dc_skip depends on carrier type:  8
if carrier is of LTE DL type and frequency_offset + startPrbc * 12 * f + k * f  ≥ 0 then dc_skip = f  9
else  dc_skip = 0. 10
The above formulation is intended to result in resource grid position in frequency compatible with 3GPP requirements, 11
defined in [12] and [13]. 12
Value range: {00 0000 0000b-11 1111 1111b}. 13
Type: unsigned integer. 14
Field length: 10 bits. 15
 16
5.4.5.5 reMask (resource element mask) 17
Description: This parameter defines the Resource Element (RE) mask within an PRB. Each bit setting in the reMask 18
indicates if the section control is applicable to the RE sent in U-Plane messages (0=not applicable; 1=applicable).  MSB 19
indicates the value for the RE of the lowest frequency in a PRB. 20
Note that different REs in a PRB may be referenced by different data section descriptions. This is restricted to data 21
section descriptions having the same sectionId but different reMask if C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via sectionId is 22
used (see 5.4.1.2.1). If C-Plane and U-Plane coupling method independent on sectionId (see 5.4.1.2.2 or 5.4.1.2.2) is 23
used, then data sections descriptions referencing different REs in a PRB must have different reMask values but 24
sectionId is not relevant. In addition, if C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via frequency and time with priorities (see 25
5.4.1.2.3) is used a RE in a PRB may be referenced by more than one data section description (in terms of reMask) but 26
only configuration carried with data section description of highest priority is applicable (see 5.4.1.2.3 and 5.4.7.6.4).  27
The the maximum number of different reMask values that may be applied to a PRB is an O-RU characteristic that is 28
conveyed from the O-RU to the O-DU via the M-Plane.  If any RE in a PRB is never pointed to by an reMask (but other 29
REs in that PRB are), the “missing” RE should be set to zero in the U-Plane, and no beamforming ID or other 30
processing should be applied to the “missing” RE.  No RE may be referenced more than once in a data section. 31
Value range: {0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111b}. 32
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 33
Field length: 12 bits. 34
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111b (all REs in the block applicable). 35
 36
5.4.5.6 numPrbc (number of contiguous PRBs per data section description) 37
Description: This parameter defines the PRBs within the data section being described. Values of startPrbc and 38
numPrbc must ensure that data sections must never overlap: a single PRB may only exist within one data section for a 39
given value of eAxC.   40
Value range: {0000 0001b-1111 1111b, 0000 0000b = all PRBs in the specified SCS and carrier bandwidth}. 41
 Value 0000 0000b is reserved for NR cases wherein the total number of PRBs may be more than 255.  In this case, 42
the sending node shall set the startPrbc value to zero and the receiving node shall ignore whatever startPrbc value is 43
received and assume it is zero. For all other cases a non-zero value of numPrbc must be used. 44
More specifically, if number of PRBs that needs to be sent is more than 255 but not all the PRBs in the specified SCS 45
and carrier bandwidth, then it is expected that multiple data sections describing smaller numner of PRBs are specified. 46
Type: unsigned integer. 47

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.

O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
Field length: 8 bits. 1
 2
5.4.5.7 numSymbol (number of symbols) 3
Description: This parameter defines number of symbols, or number of PRACH repetitions in the case of PRACH, to 4
which the section control is applicable. At minimum, the section control shall be applicable to at least one symbol. 5
However, possible optimizations could allow for several (up to 14) symbols, if e.g., all 14 symbols use the same beam 6
ID. 7
Value range: {0001b-1110b=number of symbols, 0000b=reserved, 1111b=reserved}. 8

5.4.5.8 ef (extension flag) 12

5.4.5.9 beamId (beam identifier) 20
Description: This parameter defines the beam pattern to be applied to the U-Plane data. beamId = 0 means no 21
beamforming operation will be performed. No beamforming operation implies that the RU shall not apply any phase or 22
amplitude weights to the U-plane data and that the resulting RF signal will be applied to all antenna elements in the 23
group equally. 24
Note that the beamId encodes the beamforming to be done on the O-RU.  This beamforming may be digital, analog or 25
both (“hybrid beamforming”) and the beamId provides all the information necessary for the O-RU to select the correct 26
beam (or weight table or beam attributes from which to create a beam).  It is intended that the beamId be global for the 27
O-RU meaning there are 32767 possible beams shared within the O-RU for all Rtcids/Pcids and shared between UL and 28
DL (beamId=0x0000 is reserved for no beamforming).  The specific mapping of beamId to e.g. weight table, beam 29
attributes, directionality, beam adjacency or any other beam designator is specific to the O-RU design and must be 30
conveyed via M-Plane from the O-RU to O-DU upon startup. 31
NOTE: An upper bound on the max number of beamIDs that can be addressed per eAxC or per sets of eAxCs, per 32
symbol and per slot, for DL and for UL respectively, shall be conveyed via  M-plane messaging as part of the O-RU 33
capabilities description. 34
Value range: {000 0000 0000 0001b-111 1111 1111 1111b; 000 0000 0000 0000b means no BF to be done} 35
Type: unsigned integer. 36
Field length: 15 bits. 37
Default Value: 0000 0000 0000 0000b (no beamforming). 38
 39
5.4.5.10 ueId (UE identifier) 40
Description: This parameter provides a label for the UE for which the section contents apply.  This is used to support 41
channel information sending from the O-DU to the O-RU.  This is just a label and the specific value has no meaning 42
regarding types of UEs that may be supported within the system. 43

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      92
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
Value range: {000 0000 0000 0000b-111 1111 1111 1111b} 1
Type: unsigned integer. 2
Field length: 15 bits. 3
 4
5.4.5.11 freqOffset (frequency offset) 5
Description: This parameter defines the frequency offset with respect to the carrier center frequency before additional 6
filtering (e.g. for PRACH) and FFT processing (in UL) in steps of one half the subcarrier spacings f. The frequency 7
offset shall be consistent per data section (one cannot use reMask to allow different frequency offsets for different REs 8
in the PRBs). 9
Frequency offset in Hz is calculated as: 10
 frequency_offset = freqOffset * f * 0.5 11
where f is frequency in Hz corresponding to subcarrier spacing provided in frameStructure (see 5.4.4.13). 12
Note: Frequency span resulting from frameStructure, freqOffset, startPrbc, numPrbc, and rb must not exceed channel 13
bandwidth configured for eAxC over M-plane. 14
Value range: { 0x000000=no offset,  15
0x000001 – 0x7FFFFF = positive frequency offset,  16
0x800000 – 0xFFFFFF = negative frequency offset }. 17
Type: signed integer. 18
Field length: 24 bits. 19
 20
5.4.5.12 regularizationFactor (regularization Factor) 21
Description: This parameter provides a signed value to support MMSE operation within the O-RU when beamforming 22
weights are supported in the O-RU, so related to section type 6. 23
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b} 24
Type: unsigned integer. 25
Field length: 16 bits. 26
 27
5.4.5.13 ciIsample, ciQsample (channel information I and Q values) 28
Description: These values are the channel information complex values relayed from the O-DU to the O-RU, related to 29
section type 6.  The order of transmission is first Prbc for the first antenna to the last antenna, then second Prbc for the 30
first to last antenna, and so on until reaching the last Prbc for the first to last antenna.  The bit-width per I and Q value is 31
variable (determined by M-Plane messaging) so after the very last Q value, some number of padding (set to zero) bits 32
may be inserted to get to the next byte boundary. When the optional “little endian byte order” is chosen via M-plane, the 33
ciIsample/ciQsample shall use little endian byte order to transmit the complex numbers. Refer to Annex D.1 for details. 34
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b} for each I and Q value 35
Type: signed integer. 36
Field length: variable bit-with per I and Q value. 37

5.4.5.14 laaMsgType (LAA message type) 39

message.  Note that here the C-Plane messages may flow from the O-DU to the O-RU (as usual) or from the O-RU to 41
the O-DU.  All of these messages relate to the listen-before-talk (LBT) LAA operation and provide a “handshake” 42
between the O-DU and the O-RU to manage the LBT operation. 43

5.4.5.21 lbtMode (LBT Mode) 17
Description: Part of multi-carrier support. Indicates whether full LBT process is carried or partial LBT process is 18
carried (multi carrier mode B according to 3GPP TS 36.213 Section 15.1.5.2).  19
00b = full LBT (regular LBT, sending reservation signal until the beginning of the SF/slot) 20
01b = Partial LBT (looking back 25 sec prior to transmission as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 section 15.1.5.2) 21
10b = Partial LBT (looking back 34 sec prior to transmission as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 section 15.1.5.2) 22
11b = full LBT and stop (regular LBT, do NOT send reservation signal; O-RU senses the spectrum for the defer factor 23
+ a sensing slot right before OTA when the O-DU is ready to transmit data as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 24
section 15.1.1. i.e., right before the SF/slot boundary) 25
Value range: {00b - 11b} 26

o 10b = success – indicates that the channel was successfully acquired 34
o 11b = Failure – indicates expiration of the LBT timer.  The LBT process should be reset. 35
Value range: {00b - 11b} 36

5.4.7 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Section 15
Extensions 16
5.4.7.1 ExtType=1: Beamforming Weights Extension Type 17
This section applies to the sending of beamforming weights from the O-DU to the O-RU.  When this is done, the 18
weights are sent along with a beamID which is meant to allow those same weights to be used in future C -Plane 19
messages by invoking the same beamID (without the need to send the weights again).  This allows downloaded weights 20
to have “persistence” which should save DL throughput by not requiring sending of weights multiple times.  The K 21
parameter is defined in section 10.5.2.  Refer to Annex D for details on the usual weight byte order.   The optional “little 22
endian byte order” is applied to bfwI/bfwQ fields if chosen via M-plane. Refer to Annex D.1 for details of little endian 23
byte order. This section extension applies only to section types 1 and 3. 24
Table 5-14 : Extension Type 1 Data Format 25
ef extType = 0x1 1 Octet N
extLen 1 Octet N+1
bfwCompHdr 1 Octet N+2
bfwCompParam var Octet N+3
bfwI (for TRX 0) var
bfwQ (for TRX0) var
remaining beamforming weights bfwI and bfwQ up to K TRXs var
zero pad to 4-byte boundary var
 26

Note that for the block compression methods, the block size is the entire vector of beamforming weights, not some 30
subset of them. 31
Value range: {0000 0000b-1111 1111b} 32
Bit allocations 33

This section extension applies only to section types 1 and 3 and is to be used only for LTE TM2, TM3 and TM4.  For 2

 9
There may be two or four antenna ports hence two or four beamIDs needed  (same beamID for user data and CRS REs).  10
For Antenna Port 0, the beamId is contained in the C-Plane data section header, while the Antenna Ports 1-3 beamIDs 11
are contained in this section extension.  When there are two antenna ports, the section extension  only contains the 12
second Antenna Port beam ID (“beamIdAP1”) and the section extension length is 3 words (“extLen” = 0x 3).  When 13
there are four antenna ports, the section extension contains the second, third and fourth Antenna Port beam IDs 14
(“beamIdAP1”, “beamIdAP2”. And “beamIdAP3”) and the section extension length is 4 words (“extLen” = 0x 4). 15
For the txScheme indicating TxD, one Pcid is used for all the user data and one section instantiation is needed using the 16
corresponding C-Plane Rtcid, providing all the beam IDs (up to 4) for the user data; a second section instantiation  (same 17
sectionId) with a different reMask may be used to provide the CRS RE beam IDs (also up to 4).   In the TxD case the 18
layerId is set to 1111b (“TxD”). 19
For the txSchemes indicating spatial multiplexing (LD CDD or no CDD), each layer will have its own Pcid for the user 20
data with a corresponding C-Plane Rtcid conveying the user data’s beamId, with this section extension showing a 21
different layer number for each layer.  Only within the layer ID zero Rtcid will the CRS REs be provided with their 22
beamIDs (one beamId in the section header and the other beamIDs in this section extension) . For the non-zero layer 23
number Rtcids, this section extension will still be provided to guide the precoding operation (provide the layer ID) but 24
will not include beamIds (extLen = 0x1), and the beamId in the section header should be ignored by the O-RU and 25
should be set to the default value by the O-DU. 26

5.4.7.5.1 mcScaleReMask  (modulation compression power scale RE mask) 15

type 5.  If any RE in a PRB is never pointed to by a mcScaleReMask (but other REs in that PRB are), the “missing” RE 21
should be considered to represent not populated REs (e.g. no user data to transmit). 22

mcScaleReMasks should be set (=1) in a position where the reMask has a zero, and every reMask bit that is set (=1) 24
should have exactly one bit =1 in one of the mcScaleReMasks.  If these rules are violated, the O-RU’s reaction is 25
undefined.  26

5.4.7.6 ExtType=6: Non-contiguous PRB allocation in time and frequency domain 23
This section extension applies only to Section Types 1, 3 and 5. 24
This section extension enables allocation of non-contiguous sets of PRBs (Resource Block Groups, or RBGs) in 25
frequency and time domain. This will reduce significantly the C-Plane overhead when users or channels are allocated 26
with non-contiguous sets of PRBs in time and frequency. 27
If this section extension is present in a section description then the field startSymbolId in the message header and the 28
fields rb, symInc, and numSymbol in the section description are not used for identification of symbols and PRBs 29
referred by the section description (the values of these parameters can be used by othe r section descriptions in the 30
message; note sender may set symInc and numSymbol to any allowed value without restriction to values corresponding 31
to symbols actually referred by the section description with Section Extension =6).  Sender shall set rb to the value of 32
zero. Sender shall set startSymbolId to the earliest symbol referred by any of section descriptions in the message, 33
including, but not limited to, section descriptions with Section Extension =6. The earliest symbol referenced by a 34
section description with Section Extension =6 is the earliest symbol selected by a set bit in the symbolMask. That 35
means symbolMask’s bit n, such that n < startSymbolId, must be zero. 36
Usage of this section extension does not affect the operation of user plane. It is note d that a data section in the user 37
plane is not required to contain a contiguous range of PRBs. By invoking the sectionId multiple times in the user plane, 38
either within a single message or in different messages, sets of non-contiguous PRBs can be handled. 39

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      110
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
Note that utilization of the non-contiguous PRB allocation section extension does not put any restriction on utilization 1
of sections with contiguous PRB utilization except for the general rules of utilization of sections e.g. in the context of 2
one eAxC, a resource element must be referenced by at most one data section description in the control plane. 3
In case a control plane section is cited multiple times then all citations shall allocate same set of PRBs and symbols.  4
Note that when utilizing this section extension together with Section Type 3 where freqOffset parameter is present, then 5
freqOffset affects the frequency span for the specific range of PRB numbers. 6
 7
Table 5-28: Section Format for Section Extension 6 (non-contiguous PRB allocation in time and frequency) 8
ef extType = 0x06 1 Octet N
extLen = 0x02 (2 words) 1 N+1
repetition rbgSize [2:0] rbgMask [27:24] 1 N+2
rbgMask [23:16] 1 N+3
rbgMask[15:8] 1 N+4
rbgMask[7:0] 1 N+5
priority[1:0] symbolMask[13:8] 1 N+6
symbolMask[7:0] 1 N+7
 9

5.4.7.6.1 rbgSize (resource block group size) 11
Description: This parameter indicates the size in number of PRBs of the resource block groups allocated by the bit 12
mask. The size of the resource block group to be used by the application shall be taken from the mapping table given in 13
the Value range field in the rbgMask description below. See rbgMask for special handling of exceptional resource block 14
groups. 15
Value range: {000b: reserved, 001b: 1, 010b: 2, 011b: 3, 100b: 4, 101b: 6, 110b: 8, 111b: 16}. 16
Type: unsigned integer. 17
Field length: 3 bits. 18
Default Value: 001b. 19
 20
5.4.7.6.2 rbgMask (resource block group bit mask) 21
Description: This parameter is a bit mask where each bit indicates whether a corresponding resource block group is 22
allocated. If bit n in the mask is set, then the resource block group n is allocated where  n can take values in range [0, 23
lastRbgid] where  24
lastRbgid = ceiling( (numPrbc + (startPrbc mod rbgSize))/ rbgSize ) - 1. 25
The range of PRBs included in a resource block group is given as follows 26
Resource block group 0 include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc, startPrbc+f(0)-1]. 27
Resource block group n include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc + f(0) + (n -1)*f(n), startPrbc + f(0) + n*f(n)-1] 28
where 0 < n < lastRbgid. 29
Resource block group n = lastRbgid include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc + num Prbc – f(lastRbgid), startPrbc+ 30
numPrbc -1]. 31
Where f(n) gives the number of PRBs included in resource block group n is given as follows:  32
f(0) = rbgSize – (startPrbc mod rbgSize) 33
f(n) = rbgSize, where 0<n<lastRbgid. 34
if (startPrbc + numPrbc) mod rbgsize > 0 then  f(lastRbgid) = (startPrbc + numPrbc) mod rbgSize 35

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      111
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
else  f(lastRbgid) = rbgSize 1
Only PRBs within the range defined by startPrbc and numPrbc can be allocated ie [startPrbc, numPrbc -1]. In case 2
numPrbc is zero the PRB range is all PRBs as defined by the eAxC and startPrbc shall be set to zero. Transmitter shall 3
ensure that rbgMask does not have non-zero bits outside the valid range [0, lastRbgid], if receiver detects non-zero bits 4
outside the valid range, those shall be ignored. 5
Transmitter shall ensure that combinations of startPrbc, numPrbc and rbgSize leading to a value of lastRbgid larger than 6
27 (number of bits available in the rbgMask field - 1) are never used. Such combinations are invalid and if detected by 7
the receiver the section shall be ignored. 8
MSB of rbgMask indicates the highest-frequency resource block group. 9
 10
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000 0000 0000 0000b - 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111b}. 11
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 12
Field length: 28 bits. 13
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111b (all resource block groups allocated). 14
 15
 16
Figure 5-9 Resource block group definition example. 17
 18
5.4.7.6.3 symbolMask (symbol bit mask) 19
Description: This parameter is a bit mask where each bit indicates whether the rbgMask applies to a given symbol in 20
the slot.    If bit n is set then the rbgMask is applied to symbol n, where n has range [0..13].  If no bits are set this 21
implies the rbgMask may be applied to no RBGs in the slot, in other words there are no RE allocations in the slot (or a 22
different data section contains the RE allocation for the slot).  If the symbolMask values indicate allocations beyond a 23
slot boundary, such allocations shall be ignored (e.g. when there are fewer than 14 symbols in a slot).  24
LSB of symbolMask indicates symbol zero (the first symbol to arrive in a slot). 25
Value range: {00 0000 0000 0000b-11 1111 1111 1111b}. 26
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 27
Field length: 14 bits. 28
Default Value: 11 1111 1111 1111b (section repeated in 14 symbols). 29
 30
5.4.7.6.4 priority 31
Description: This parameter is used in conjunction with C-Plane and U-Plane coupling via frequency and time with 32
priorities (see 5.4.1.2.3). If this coupling method is not used (e.g. O -RU or O-DU do not have corresponding capability) 33
sender shall send value zero. This parameter is used by O-RU to find the section description with the highest priority 34
among section descriptions referencing the same RE that are present in one C -Plane message. O-RU restricts the scope 35
of the search one C-plane message to avoid beamforming configuration errors that would occur if search would span 36
multiple messages and one of them was lost. If section extension type #6 is absent, then data section description priority 37
is zero (this corresponds to the default priority). Within one C-plane message a set of priority values is restricted to up 38
to two priority values including value zero i.e. {0, +1} or {0, -1}. 39
Value -2 is reserved and shall not be used by sender. 40

5.4.7.6.5 repetition (repetition flag) 5
Description: This parameter is used to indicate repetition of a highest priority data section inside a C-Plane message. 6
This is an optional field for O-RU i.e. when the highest priority section is repeated in a C-Plane message O-DU should 7
set this flag, however O-RU can choose to process or ignore this flag. This field is applicable only when extension type 8
6 is used with coupling via frequency and time with priorities (Optimized) for highest priority section descriptions 9
(since they are repeated across C-Plane messages). 10

5.4.7.7 ExtType=7: eAxC Mask Section Extension 15
This section extension is meant to allow a specific C-Plane message to apply not to just a single eAxC value but to 16
multiple eAxC values.  The intended use case applies to Section Type 0, wherein the intention is to allow blanking 17
(designated by Section Type 0) to be indicated for multiple eAxC values e.g. all component carriers.   Table 5-29 shows 18
the section extension format. 19
Table 5-29 : Section Format for Section Extension 7 (eAxC Mask parameter) 20
ef extType = 0x07 1 Octet N
extLen = 0x01 (1 word) 1 N+1
eAxCmask[15:8] 1 N+2
eAxCmask[7:0] 1 N+3
 21
When a C-Plane message with this Section Extension is received by an O-RU, the O-RU should react as if multiple C-22
Plane messages were received with all of the eAxC values permitted by the mask.  Note that using the mask, it is 23
possible the O-RU may assume the C-Plane message content applies to eAxC values that are not intended and are not 24
used (e.g. if two bits of the mask are set to zero to indicate the message applies to all 3 sectors, there will be a non-25
existent fourth sector that will be implied too).  In this case there will be no U -Plane data specified for the spurious 26
eAxC value(s) and the O-RU should not consider this as an error. 27
Support of this Section Extension is optional: if an O-RU reports a capability excluding support of this Section 28
Extension then the O-DU must not employ it, and if the O-DU does not support this section extension the same effect 29
can be obtained using multiple single-eAxC C-Plane messages so no functionality is lost (though the C-Plane will be 30
less efficient).  31
5.4.7.7.1 eAxCmask (eAxC Mask) 32
Description: This binary mask indicates which eAxC values the C-Plane message applies to.  A “0” bit in the mask 33
means the specified eAxC bit is “don’t care” while a “1” bit in the mask means the specified eAxC bit should be 34
considered.  An all-zero eAxCmask means “use this message for all eAxC values” while an all-ones eAxCmask means 35
“use this message for only the designated eAxC value”.  In the former ca se (“use this message for all eAxC values”), 36
the actual eAxC value in the C-Plane message header could be any value because the message would apply to all eAxC 37
values regardless of the actual value in the C-Plane message.  In the latter case (“use this message for only the 38
designated eAxC value”) this section extension adds no value because that is the normal operation.  39
The intended use of the mask is to indicate which sub-field of the eAxC the message applies to.  For example, if a single 40
sector single band of the O-RU will be blanked for all component carriers, the RU-Port-ID and CC-ID sub-field 41
portions of the eAxCmask would be all zeros (“use this message for all layers/spatial streams and all component 42
carriers”) while the other subfield portions of the eAxCmask would be all ones (“use this message for the specific band, 43

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.      113
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v05.00
sector, and DU_Port_ID values provided in the eAxC”).  In this way a Section Type 0 message could indicate the 1
blanking of all component-carriers in a band-sector in a single C-Plane message. 2
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b}. 3
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 4
Field length: 16 bits. 5
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111 1111b (all bits of eAxC are considered). 6

5.4.7.8 ExtType=8: Regularization factor 8
This section extension is for regularizationFactor which is used to generate MU beamforming weight for the scheduled 9
UEs in a slot. regularizationFactor is the noise variance used for MMSE (Minimum Mean Square Error) computation of 10
generating MU BFW. The intended use case applies to Section Type 5 for sending regularization factor instead of 11
sending regularization factor over Section Type 6. 12
Support of this Section Extension is mandatory for O-RUs supporting Section Type 5 in this version of the 13
specification. If an O-RU reports a capability excluding support of this Section Extension (O-RUs supporting previous 14
version of specification or O-RUs not supporting Section Type 5), then the O-DU must not employ it, and if the O-RU 15
reports a capability including support of this section extension then O-DU supporting this version of specification must 16
employ this section extension instead Section Type 6 to convey regularization factor.  17
See Annex J for further description of the regularization factor’s use in UL and DL. 18

5.4.7.10 ExtType=10: Section description for group configuration of multiple ports 17
This section extension applies to section types 1, 3 and 5. C-plane section information for the multiple ports (i.e., layers 18
or Tx/Rx paths) may be the same except beam IDs or UE IDs in most cell scheduling case. When the multiple ports 19
share the common section information within O-RU, C-plane sections to be sent via the corresponding ports are merged 20
into a C-plane section via a specified port using this section extension. M-plane pre-configures to group the ports to be 21
merged and to specify the port to represent them. The beam ID in the section of the representative port can be 22
considered an index which indicates a set of multiple beam vectors (beam IDs) each of which applies to the 23
corresponding port (layer or Tx/Rx path). 24

5.4.7.10.3 Interaction with other Section Extensions 19
Section Extension =10 can be used in all situations when same information is present in section headers and in section 20
extension headers across multiple eAxC IDs.  21
Table 5-34 : Section Extension =10 Interactions with other Section Extensions 22
Section
Extension Title Interaction with existing Section Extensions
1 Beamforming
Weights
SE1 can be used with Section Extension =10 only if the Beamforming Weights transferred
using Section Extension =1 are the same for all streams (or layers). In general, the BF
weight vector will be different per data layer (eAxC) and Section Extension =10 cannot be
used in conjunction. Once the Beamforming Weights are downloaded, then if the O -DU
uses same BF vector by addressing Beam Id for a number of slots after the BF Weight is
downloaded, then in that case, O-DU can use Section Extension 10 to combine multiple C-
plane messages to one single C-plane message using the representative eAxC id.
2 Beamforming
Attributes
Section Extension =2 can be used with Section Extension =10 only if the Beamforming
Attribute transferred using Section Extension =2is same for all streams (or layers),
otherwise, Section Extension =2 cannot be used with Section Extension =10. If O-DU uses
beam attributes downloaded using Section Extension =2 later using beam id, then Section
Extension =10 can be used to combine multiple C-plane messages to one C-plane message.
3 DL Precoding
This Section Extension has different format for different layers (first layer has one set of
parameters and rest of the layers have different set of parameters). So this Section
Extension =3 cannot be used with the Section Extension =10. There is a possibility of using
the Section Extension =10 with layers other than first layer (if the codebook index is same
for other layers) and also combining Section Extension =3 for all layers in future with some
changes. This is FSS.
4 Modulation
Compression
Section Extension =4 can be used with Section Extension =10 only if the modulation order,
and hence the same parameter values for Section Extension =4 for all streams (or layers)
apply, otherwise, Section Extension =4 cannot be used with Section Extension =10.

Modulation

(Additional)

and hence the same parameter values for Section Extension =5 for all streams (or layers)
apply, otherwise, Section Extension =5 cannot be used with Section Extension =10

extensions present in the section description) divided by numBundPrb. When the division outcome is fractional value, 15
one additional beamforming weight for each respective TRX is included to cover the orphan PRBs. The value zero is 16
reserved. 17

5.4.7.11.7 RAD (Reset After PRB Discontinuity) 3
Description: This parameter is used when section extension =11 is used in conjunction with section extension allowing 4

5.4.7.12 ExtType=12: Non-Contiguous PRB Allocation with Frequency Ranges 16
This section extension applies only to Section Types 1, 3 and 5. It cannot be used with section extension 6 in the same 17
section description. 18
This section extension enables allocation of non-contiguous sets of PRBs (Resource Block Groups, or RBGs) in time 19
domain and frequency domain. This extension reduces the C-Plane overhead when users or channels are allocated with 20
non-contiguous sets of PRBs in time or frequency. This extension is more space-efficient than Section Extension 6 if 21
the allocation is continuous in frequency or extends over a frequency span wider than the range defined by rbgMask 22
size and rbgMaskSize value. 23
Table 5-36: Section Format for Section Extension 12 Non-Contiguous PRB Allocation with Frequency Ranges  24

This extension consists of a fixed part (fields priority and symbolMask) and a variable size part (pairs of offStartPrb(r) 26
and numPrb(r) for r = 1 … R-1). Note that variable part may be empty allowing to use priority and symbolMask without 27
overhead. 28
If this section extension is present in a section description, then the section description is applied to symbols identified 29
by symbolMask and one or more frequency ranges calculated from startPrbc and numPrbc from the  section description 30
and offStartPrb(r) and numPrb(r) pairs from this extension. 31
If this section extension is present in a section description, then the field startSymbolId in the message header and the 32
fields rb, symInc, and numSymbol in the section description are not used for identification of symbols and PRBs 33
referred by the section description (the values of these parameters can be used by other section descriptions in the 34
